Chronicle

Imperial Incense Misty Records 288

— Original Work by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

As mentioned above, all female officials were daughters of high-ranking Manchu officials; my younger sister Rongling and I were the beloved daughters of Duke Yugeng. My father received orders from the court very early to serve as ambassador to various countries: therefore, we received Western education from an early age. Please forgive my boasting! At that time, there were truly very few women like us who were able to understand foreign languages: therefore, the Empress Dowager valued us sisters particularly highly; and others envied us to the extreme! Although there were no special titles such as "Chief Female Official" at the time, in fact, we could indeed be regarded as leaders of all female officials.

Two of the female officials were daughters of Prince Qing. At that time, Prince Qing was serving as Minister of Military Affairs, so naturally he was also a very, very big official! There was also a Shun Wang Consort. Speaking of this person's background, it was also very significant. She and Empress Longyu were biological sisters, and the Empress Dowager was also her aunt, so the relationship should have been very close: the reason she was selected to enter the palace and serve as a female official was because the Empress Dowager wanted to give some benefits to her own relatives. In this case, the Empress Dowager must have been very considerate of her own relatives. However, the opposite was true! I don't know why! I still haven't understood it until now, or perhaps it was a kind of neuropsychiatric disorder! She hated those members of the imperial family and her own mother's family, those close relatives, with a vengeance. Although she held all the power in China and could change any official at will, she never allowed any of her relatives to hold a position that was relatively important and easy to make money; therefore, all relatives who had a direct relationship with her, except for a very small minority, were mostly as poor as the lower class.

One more thing worth mentioning is that before her death, the Empress Dowager felt especially bitter animosity towards Puyi! That is, Puyi who is currently working as a "puppet" for the Japanese in the three northeastern provinces (Translator's note: The author's original text also writes "Japan's Puppet" in large letters, which can give Europeans and Americans a deep impression, which is gratifying. Gratifying.)! Whenever someone mentioned them, she would frown and be unhappy. (87)

A Record of a Strange Old Woman 289

— >Qing Shou

In our Jiading area, there is an old woman in Dongli who, to tell the truth, is strange: readers, don't think that I am making up a fictitious story, but in fact it is very true, without any embellishment; the old woman's surname is Zhu, and she is already over seventy years old. When her old man was alive, he had a moderate amount of property, but he was extremely stingy, and he would not spend a penny on anything in vain; even if he sold a copper coin's worth of tofu, he would divide it into two days to eat. For example, today he would first pay a copper coin, take only five coins' worth of tofu, and have half left to take tomorrow; can you imagine! Isn't he an economic expert? What's strange is that in the year before the old man died, he suddenly started a major construction project, building a high-hall large house, but unfortunately, not many days after its completion, death descended, and he became a guest of the heavenly court; moreover, he had no biological children, so all the real estate and land were naturally enjoyed by the collateral branches of the same clan; now, the old woman! Only a pair of old bones is left, and she seems to be suffering a tragic fate of loneliness and isolation. What is the reason for this? Such an old person's temperament naturally would not be harmonious with the daughters-in-law, so she had to live alone; it is said that these days, when the temperature reaches one hundred and four degrees, how afraid of heat is the old woman, but the upper half of her body is already naked, and she is holding cotton trousers in her hand, her feet are on a burning red copper stove, and she is still shouting that her feet are cold; those who don't know would think she is suffering from mental illness, but in fact, although she is old, her mind is still one hundred and twenty points clear! Some people say that her upper body is living in summer, and her lower body is still living in winter. If we talk about her unique physiology, we might as well determine that she has a double personality, so I wrote her out to offer readers a smile.

Rural Night Scene 290

— Ding

As soon as the sun sets, the fields are bustling with activity, and it's the farmers' happy time to go home and rest.

The men use coarse cloth dipped in river water to wipe away the dirt on their bodies on the river bank. All the fatigue and exhaustion have been washed away with the dirt. A low platform made of a board and four wooden strips is placed in front of each house; a dish of salted broad beans, a bamboo basket of cold rice, and a small jar of iced tea, which is refreshing and simple. As long as you take a glance at how they eat, you will surely believe that these things taste much better than the delicacies of mountains and seas in the city.

Sparks flying out of the pile of firewood are flashing like fireflies on the edge of the field. The cool breeze of the summer night brings lightness and comfort. The old people are chatting idly without any restrictions with their water pipes; starting from the enthronement of Emperor Xuantong, they talk about the trivial sesame seed and mung bean matters in the village. Sometimes even those moldy and rotten past events of years or decades ago will be revived in their dry toothless mouths. The young men lie naked on the door panels looking at the clear sky, and in the blue sky are the smiles of the girls they yearn for. The children are chopping the grass that will be fed to the plowing cattle tomorrow, and of course there are bound to be quarrels with each other. Mixed with shy laughter, what makes people feel a special flavor is that those innocent village girls are learning to sing love songs that they occasionally hear from the city. I say that the rural night scene in early summer is a picture full of poetic meaning.

Fourth Company Commander of Northeast 291

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirty-Two Enjoying Themselves With Singing and Dancing The General Enjoys Himself All Day, Old and Young Sobbing, How Many Soldiers Return

After eight o'clock, suddenly the sounds of silk strings, drums, and clappers were noisy, and the voices of men and women singing the ballad book continued until two o'clock in the evening before stopping. Guizhi thought to herself that it was just a rich family, with some happy event at home, enjoying themselves at any time, and she didn't pay attention to it. The next morning, she put the newly moved-in set of small stove in the yard and swept it with a long broom. Suddenly, a person stretched a head out from the side yard door and smiled, "Oh! A new neighbor has moved in." Guizhi looked at the woman, wearing a blue cloth short fur coat and a blue cloth apron, like a maid from a high-class family, so she nodded and said, "We are new here. Do you live here too?" The woman pointed to the Western-style building upstairs and said, "Look! I live upstairs." Guizhi smiled, "Oh! Then we are really neighbors. Did you have something happy at your mansion last night?" The woman said, "No! Why do you ask?" Guizhi said, "I heard singing and playing upstairs until late at night, so I guessed that way." The woman smiled, "That's nothing. When our concubine throws a tantrum, she wants the moon, and our division commander doesn't dare to give her the stars. It's funny to say, last night, our division commander came back a little late and missed dinner. He originally said he would take the concubine to eat at a restaurant and listen to a play, but he made the concubine wait for a while. She was unyielding and just threw a temper tantrum. No matter how carefully the division commander coaxed her, it was no use. The division commander had no choice but to find a group of ballad singers to make noise at home for the whole night, and that was considered relieving the concubine's boredom." Ms. Jiang was also in the kitchen next door, also gossiping. Hearing this, she also teased, "This is really new." The woman said, "It's not new..." She still wanted to explain the reason why it wasn't new, but because someone in the front shop was calling, the woman left. Here, the mother and daughter were taking care of things in the kitchen, chatting idly. Guizhi smiled, "Listen, rich people are too good at enjoying themselves, with nothing to do, they just sing and make noise at home. I say, the Western-style building across the street is too lively, it turns out they are a division commander." (438)

Bo Xi Sound 292

— Wei Jing

One night, it was already after three o'clock, and Mr. Wang in the parlor building was going home through the back door. Although Mr. Wang had a proper job, because he was addicted to gambling, drinking, and whoring outside, his family's finances were very tight, and this was the main reason why he and his wife often quarreled and fought.

That night, Mr. Wang returned home in the middle of the night, constantly yawning, eager to restore the fatigue of not sleeping well for several nights, but Mrs. Wang refused to let him off lightly, so when Mr. Wang had just taken off his hat, she stretched out her hand and asked him for the rent and food expenses that had been overdue.

Although these are necessities of life in every family, Mr. Wang's pockets were empty, because that night, Mr. Wang had lost all the money in his pockets. There was no money in his pocket, and he couldn't deal with it, so Mrs. Wang began to sob.

Mr. Wang had already been feeling sullen because he had lost in gambling, and now seeing Mrs. Wang crying, he simply opened his mouth and started scolding people. Mrs. Wang had already suffered grievances, and at this point she began to cry to the heavens and wail loudly. This was followed by the crisp sound of slaps, the heavy sound of throwing objects, mixed with the terrified cries of the child after being awakened, calling for her mother, all mixed together. The four or five families living together were all吵得unable to fall asleep. But no one was happy to come up to dissuade them, because it had been staged this way repeatedly in the past.

Four o'clock, five o'clock, crying and闹一直 until dawn, Mr. Wang left hatefully, Mrs. Wang was still crying.

Small Cookbook

Relief from Summer Heat Soup 293

— Wei Yongchi

Mung beans, according to the "Materia Medica," are mild and can relieve summer heat and quench thirst. Drinking its juice in summer prevents many diseases. I don't use mung bean soup for a reason. There is also a reason for relief from summer heat soup. It's because in "Dream of the Red Chamber," there's a passage about the characters' deep emotions: Daiyu and Baoyu each have secrets in their hearts, but they are difficult to express. Now, Baoyu hears Daiyu say the words "good marriage" and becomes even more contrary. He angrily grits his teeth, takes off the jade pendant around his neck, throws it, and smashes it. Daiyu is even more anxious when she sees him smashing that dumb thing. Fortunately, Xiren rushes to take it away and jokingly persuades Baoyu, "You and your sister are quarreling; there's no need to smash it. If it's smashed, how will she be able to face people?" When Daiyu hears this, it strikes a chord in her heart. It shows that Baoyu isn't even as good as Xiren, and she begins to cry even more sadly. Being troubled, she can't even handle the relief from summer heat soup she just drank and vomits it up. From this, we can see that in the Grand View Garden, mung bean soup is also used to relieve summer heat. I have excerpted it here to prove that mung bean soup can relieve summer heat, and even Lin Daiyu drinks it, showing its true value. Therefore, I don't use the title "Mung Bean Soup," but borrow the title "Relief from Summer Heat Soup" to cleverly choose a title, as it was vomited up along with the fragrant saliva from her mouth. Enough of idle talk; let's get back to the main topic.

Mung bean soup is a food that, every summer, regardless of rich or poor, large or small households, is consumed because it is inexpensive and beneficial, and also because of customs. Before the use of cold drinks from abroad led to the spread of diseases, southerners, in addition to considering watermelon a good companion for relieving summer heat, considered this the best method for relieving summer heat. But once autumn arrives, people fear getting diarrhea from eating watermelon and stop eating it. If an Indian summer arrives, they still use this as a remedy. However, there are great differences in how mung bean soup and mung bean porridge are cooked. Here are the results of my research to share with readers:

It is said that an essential condition for mung bean soup is that the amount of water added during the initial cooking must be precise. For example, to make a soup with one liter of mung beans, you must add three and a half or four liters of water, which is just right. If you are cooking mung bean porridge, because you add a handful of rice, you must have four full liters of water. Whether it's soup or porridge, you must use high heat at first until it boils, then reduce the heat to simmer it through, until the beans are fully bloomed. Then, use domestic cane sugar, blend it well, and after it comes out of the pot, drink it slightly cooled. It tastes excellent. The worst thing is to not add enough water at the beginning and then add water when it's partially cooked, as its taste is completely different from that of the ones without adding water. If you don't believe me, try it, and you'll know it's true.

Summer's Economical Drinks 294

— Linghu Zhao

As the saying goes, "When hungry, think of food; when thirsty, think of drink." "Drink" and "food" are two necessities of life. In noble Shanghai, the general working-class people are very "careful" about both food and drink because their finances don't allow them to spend recklessly! For example, in dance halls and restaurants, a bowl of mung bean soup or a cup of iced coffee costs one yuan, while those frozen oranges sold by peddlers on the street are expensive, so the average working class doesn't dare to eat or drink them. Although the latter are cheap, they are harmful to health. Therefore, I have recorded several extremely economical, hygienic, and beneficial drinks to offer to readers.

(1) Barley Tea: Roast one liter of barley in a pot until it turns brown, preserving its properties. Steep in boiling water. It has the fragrant taste of coffee, but none of the bitterness of tea leaves. It can clear the mind and awaken the spleen, preventing summer heat. It is beneficial and harmless to drink often in summer.

(2) Honeysuckle Dew: Buy a handful of honeysuckle and chrysanthemum at a pharmacy, add one or two fresh spearmint leaves, and one or two slices of licorice. Steep in boiling water. After it cools, it has a sweet and pleasant taste. It can eliminate summer heat, and drinking it for a long time can prevent boils.

(3) Chrysanthemum Tea: Steep a handful of dried chrysanthemum flowers with a little white sugar (not too much, as too much will be too sweet and harmful) in boiling water. After it cools, drink it. It is cooling and fragrant, and its effect is the same as honeysuckle dew.

(4) Cold Boiled Water: Boil clear water and let it cool before drinking. It is more beneficial than street drinks.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

The Thorough Liberation of Women's Professions 295

— Qian Xu

Everyone must admit that Chinese society is still a male-dominated society.

In name or on the surface, women have already been liberated. There are female members of the Central Committee, female civil servants, female employees, and female workers. In politics, economics, and education, women and men supposedly have equal opportunities and equal rights, and it seems that a truly equal state has been achieved.

But in reality, we can see that the underside of women's professions (including civil servants, employees, etc.) is covered with a thick layer of "decorations," "shop signs," and other colors, making them inevitably reduced to "flower vases." Is this the fault of women themselves? Thousands of years of male-dominated society have limited women's consciousness. Feudal poisons have determined women's fate. In some corners of the world, women are still bought and sold as commodities, and beautiful faces are used as a means of attracting customers. The view of women as commodities is still unavoidable.

The so-called "pleasure professions" of dancing girls are not for everyone. At the very least, they must possess the following conditions: (1) a beautiful face, (2) a slender figure, (3) the ability to go to extremes in decoration and affectation. Of course, there are other conditions, but there is no need to list them all. In short, it is only necessary to be able to win the love of a large number of men, satisfy every man's desire, and obtain a rich price. Therefore, the so-called "women in pleasure professions" are nothing more than "sexual commodities."

The tide of the global economic panic has shaken every corner, making it impossible for many women to live peacefully at home. At the same time, some women see the future crisis and try their best to shout out "women's liberation!" At the same time, some men also feel that the burden is too heavy, and there is a risk that they will not be able to bear it in the future, so they also shout "women should be liberated." Women who have been oppressed for thousands of years will naturally find it difficult to please when they want to compete and win in a "male-dominated society."

However, women are as complex as men in society. No matter how fast the wheel of the times turns, no matter how many women are abandoned far away, no matter how many women fall into the abyss of commodities, at the same time, many women are running ahead of the times, working hard and struggling.

The reason why women flow into "commodities" is, as Mr. "Bo'er" said, "the inadequacy of the social system." However, it cannot be corrected by Mr. "Xin's" simple "breaking vanity" and "promoting thrift" because, once you have become a capitalist's "commodity," you are not allowed to freely "break" or "promote." Because "breaking" means breaking your own rice bowl, and frugality will cut off your profession. This is a conflict of interest with the capitalists. This, of course, does not mean that working women should not be thrifty, but rather that this is possible under this situation.

At the same time, it is even more difficult than ascending to heaven for working women in a subordinate position (including women seeking employment) to demand absolute economic independence, especially in this society of frequent disasters, national economic bankruptcy, and widespread unemployment.

It is certainly not a matter for women alone to reform the inadequacy of the entire social system. However, to demand the liberation of women's professions, the "male-dominated society" must be changed into a "gender-shared society."

Confined or Drifting? 296

— Hong Ben

Brother ××:

I have received your letter full of grief for a long time. Why haven't I replied? It's not because I'm busy. I'm bored beyond words. Because school is on vacation, and I don't want to engage in other pursuits, so I'm naturally very idle. But why am I even too lazy to reply to your letter? This makes me feel very difficult. Because the question you raised is really too serious: is it better to stick to your homeland or to drift outside?

This is a serious question. I thought about it for a long time before I came to a decision. Now I will write it down:

Originally, there are now many people shouting, "Go back to the countryside," and "Go to the people." The former seems to have started recently, probably because the countryside has become so bankrupt in recent years that they believe that if China is to have a solution in the future, it must start with the revival of the countryside, so some people shouted this slogan. The latter is indeed an old tune, a slogan of those literary people. In this way, those who have already drifted outside should return to their nests. So, what illusions do you have who are originally in the nest? Stay put, fugitives, stay put!

However, that's not the case. My opinion is exactly the opposite. Oh, brother ××, hearing this, I imagine you must be smiling approvingly and drawing me as a close friend! Yes, this is not my speculation. Why do I not advocate that you stick to your homeland? Why do I agree to drift outside? I don't just have a conclusion without a premise. Let's look at my arguments below!

Didn't you say yourself that your hometown is so dangerous, the people are so cold, everyone thinks that you have studied at the university, so they all look at you like a dragon, but in fact, you are so disappointing to them, because you cannot be promoted and get rich because you have studied at the university, to prove that their theory that reading is useful. And you can't even make elegiac couplets, so they look down on you so much. How can you stick with that?

If you were rich, it would be easier to plan. You can have old rice to eat yourself, close the door and sit at home, pretending to be blind and deaf, ignoring people's jokes and scolding. That would be fine.

However, if that were really the case, it would be too depressing to lose the meaning of life. The dark world and chaotic society desperately need us to transform it. However, the fact is so cruel, how easy is it to transform? If you want to shoulder this responsibility with your own strength, it will not only not help the facts, but also plunge yourself into the abyss. Because this is not a branch issue, nor a people issue, but the entire social system issue. If the big premise has no way out, how can you talk about branches? Isn't it bound to hit a wall! And now, the power of the old forces in the countryside is even stronger than before, enough to lead young people astray at any time. Moreover, if you are really rich, you will basically fall by yourself.

Unfortunately, and also best of all, you are not only not rich, but you are actually penniless. From your letter, I can see that even with the low standard of living in the countryside, you are almost experiencing the crisis of "being in a difficult situation." Since you are so poor, what do you still love about your homeland? Looking closely at your tone, it seems that you have some resentment towards your own destiny. In fact, this is wrong. In this vast world, there are countless people who are as destitute as you. This responsibility clearly rests with society.

I think, friend, you should drift outside. You can only drift outside. But if you ask me what certainty there is in coming outside, what way out is there? Then I will honestly say that there are indeed no concrete benefits either. But I always feel that a living young person is better off starving to death in a foreign land than being poor at home. I have always held this idea. From the age of sixteen to now, I have been drifting for a full eight years. Although I have starved, I have still survived. And in terms of spirit, knowledge, and everything else, I have indeed gained a lot of benefits.

That's why I am persuading you to go outside. I feel that a modern young person should fully taste

Yes, it is necessary to accept a lesson in wandering. I also feel that so-called wandering, drifting, is not just a bad thing. On the other hand, it is harboring infinite truths and infinite progressive consciousness.

Brother ××, my dear friend, what are you going to do? I have babbled such a big set of things. Is it really to your taste? Does it match your views? Finally, I have one sentence to say. The world and society are never forever dark and forever chaotic. There will always be a day when light is released, over, I wish you health. Your friend, Hong Ben

In Memory of Liu Bannong 297

— Maohua

Chinese phonology expert Dr. Liu Fu died at 2:10 PM on the 14th of this month at Peking Union Medical College Hospital. People in academic circles, both well-known and unknown, across the country are writing articles of mourning, expressing their sorrow. Because I have the bond of being from the same hometown as Dr. Liu Fu, I know a little about his life, so I would like to talk about his early years of diligent study.

Liu Fu, also known as Bannong, lived in Sanjiali, Dongxiang, Jiangyin. However, his father moved to Xidajie in the city. After graduating from Liyan School, he went to Changzhou Fifth Middle School to study. Because he had some talent, he did not submit to the guidance of those old-fashioned teachers, so he did not graduate. After leaving Fifth Middle School, he came to Shanghai to translate novels (at that time, he signed his name as Liu Bannong, which was quite like a "Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies" style). Until now, we can still buy Liu's translated novels "Cat Detective," "Secret History of Continental Europe," "Account in the Tent," and "Black Shoulder Scarf" at the Zhonghua Book Company. Soon, he was appreciated by Cai Yuanpei, the president of Peking University, who felt it was a pity that he was stranded in Shanghai, so he asked him to work in the Peking University Library. There, Mr. Liu Fu had the opportunity to come into contact with the vast sea of learning. Needless to say, the foundation for becoming a specialized scholar was laid at that time.

As Mr. Liu Fu's knowledge improved, President Cai Yuanpei asked him to be a teaching assistant at Peking University. However, due to a lack of qualifications, he was occasionally ridiculed by students who were too high and mighty. Naturally, Mr. Liu Fu did not do it. By chance, with the help of President Cai Yuanpei, he went to study in France.

I don't remember clearly whether it was five or six years in that country. Mr. Liu Fu obtained a French state-recognized doctorate in literature and returned to China. It is said that the French state-recognized doctorate in literature was still the first in the Far East, which is to say that even Japan, which is bright in academics, did not have it. At that time, there was a war in our Jiangyin. The Feng Army bombed the Binta built by Wu Guotai (Sun Quan's mother). However, it did not completely bomb it, but only bombed half of the spire. The upper half of the spire looked like a pen tip, so the local people said, "Jiangyin has produced a foreign champion!" And the so-called foreign champion, of course, refers to Dr. Liu Fu.

Mr. Liu Fu was a famous doctor. Universities would naturally compete to recruit him, fearing that they would be too late. It was truly incomparable to when he had not gone abroad. During this time, Dr. Liu Fu personally participated in the May Fourth Movement, using the pen name Liu Bannong to write and promote with novelists Lu Xun, etc., and using his spare time from studying phonology to write poems in dialect (such as the famous Wafu Collection). As a result, Liu Bannong became a well-known poet and writer.

But unfortunately, Mr. Liu Bannong passed away in his prime! Mr. Chen Zizhan believes that this is a major loss in the construction of the mass language issue, and I share the same feeling.

Seeing Mr. Liu Bannong's life experience, without any further explanation, we can know how hard-working and diligent he was. And his younger brother, Mr. Tianhua, was the same. As a teacher in a small school who couldn't even play the piano, he became a German doctor of music and became one of China's most famous musicians! If it weren't for diligent study, how would he have achieved success?

However, their brothers passed away one after another, which makes us offer our infinite condolences.

When the Whistle Blows 298

— Chen Yi

When the whistle blew, the sun's red face was already covered by the sharp top of the Great Coal Mountain. A thick black shadow covered this vast plain. The sun-baked river water and the white smoke of the round fields gradually

Page 21

reduced its heat. The birds in the forest also began to fly in flocks in the sky.

When the whistle blew, the distant villages, the scattered huts on the plains, and countless messy chimneys were all emitting wisps of thick smoke, winding around the roofs. The yellow-faced village women and the thin children, some holding shovels and bamboo baskets, and some holding hoes and water buckets, were in the fields, in the forests, collecting their firewood and food, and irrigating their wheat fields and vegetable gardens.

When the whistle blew, the street lying beside the railway gradually became lively; the people coming and going included workers and village women, old people and children. The shop assistants in the stores were shouting loudly, and the waiters in the teahouses were moving around to greet customers. Of the twenty-four hours in a day, only this moment is a lively world. The silent air became noisy, and the stagnant money flowed everywhere.

When the whistle blew, the chains of the elevator spun incessantly, and one small car after another of coal was hoisted from underground to the side of the mountain. The workers doing the transportation work were all waving beads of sweat. Pushing the coal cars that weighed two hundred pounds, they didn't care that they were covered in sweat, and they forgot that they were barefoot on the coal dust on the ground. It was only because the last train was about to depart, and the empty carriages were waiting for them to transport coal to fill them.

When the whistle blew, a group of workers stood around the elevator. The workers who were going to work were chatting cheerfully about their lives, some eating the hardened biscuits and steamed buns. But those who were going off work were all covered in coal dust and sweat, tiredly bowing their heads and panting, holding up the dimly lit carbide lamps, and dragging their heavy steps on their way home.

When the whistle blew, everything within these few miles of people and things was shaken.

Peach 299

— Cun Yin

The peach tree bore fruit.

How happy Asheng was in his heart!

Sprouting, flowering, bearing fruit... selling, making money, buying rice, filling his belly... He thought about these things every day.

This time, he saw many peaches hanging on the peach tree. Ah, how lucky he should be!

Before they were ripe, he had already picked them. He carefully packed them one by one into a basket, and couldn't bear not to eat one himself.

There were only four trees, and he had to rely on them to live for a year.

He was so old, it was fortunate that his body was not too sick.

He picked a good day to carry the load to the city. Along the way, he thought about many things. He even thought about buying a silk short shirt with the remaining money! He also thought about hiring a mason to repair the leaks in his old house.

He also hated his untrimmed long hair and beard.

Some of the peaches were red. The rest were not very ripe. They had all left their hometown and were left for people to eat. In their little hearts, perhaps they would resent people for being too brutal!

Asheng shed a lot of sweat and finally stopped in a lively place.

After wiping his sweat, he opened his broken

throat and shouted...

"Want to buy peaches? Sweet peaches!..."

Almost everyone who passed by his load of peaches at least glanced at him. Because his voice was so pitiful! And also unusually calm.

From morning to noon, he only got twenty or so copper coins.

His old heart was already panicking!

The sun was violently shining on the street. It also shone on the muscles of every hard-working person. Only those in the cars were comfortably living their luxurious dreams.

Dusk was near! He kept shouting.

How anxious he was in his heart! Although he could come out to sell again tomorrow!

When his throat could not make a sound, the sun had already escaped.

He sighed and carried the heavy load back.

Not eating for a day was not unusual for him.

The next day, he carried the load to the city again in the morning.

The sun had not yet climbed to the top of his head.

A policeman interfered with him with a stick.

"This is the place to walk! You can't..."

"Sir, small business people..."

He frowned and begged in a pitiful way.

"No way! The police raised his stick and hit him."

Suddenly, a red mark appeared on Asheng's back. He pressed on the painful area and knelt down.

"Sir, poor people... need to eat..."

"Carry it away quickly! Otherwise..."

"Sir..."

Asheng went up to hug his leg and begged.

Unexpectedly, a kick! The leather shoe with nails! It kicked him right in the chest.

He was in extreme pain! He quickly carried it away.

Running home. He was already panting very badly!

He just passed out like that.

When he woke up, he vomited many blood clots, staining his lower beard red.

He didn't know what was going on.

"I didn't rob money or kill anyone...?"

He often asked himself lightly...

A few days later, the unripe peaches in the basket were rotting!

Flies 300

— Bin Fu

For the past few days, I have been extremely frustrated and irritable. At night, I can't sleep well due to the threat of heat and the torment of bedbugs. During the day, I try to find a shady spot to lie down on a rattan chair for a nap, but those red-headed, sesame-sized fly "generals" refuse to let me go. They insist on buzzing and crawling all over my face, ears, armpits, and between my toes, incessantly buzzing and stinging.

Especially when I am just about to drift off to sleep, these creatures unexpectedly land on any part of my body and take a bite, causing me to jump up suddenly and break out in a sweat. By the time I grab a banana leaf fan to swat at them, they have already zipped away without a trace. This endless torment has left me both laughing and crying, and I am almost driven to madness.

During meals, before people have even sat down, those generals have already rudely landed on the food. If you shoo them away, they will madly make a big circle in the air, and it's impossible to track where they go. After circling, they seem to think that you are no longer chasing them, and then quickly fly back to squat on the corner of the table or in the center of the bowl. What's even more annoying is when you have just picked up a small dish of side dishes and are about to put it in your mouth, that red-headed fly happens to land on the dish, and you have to put down the side dish and chase away the fly. Isn't this kind of disgusting disruption enough to make people uncomfortable?

This is just in terms of their superficial actions, which are already enough to make us so disgusted. If we look at them from a scientific perspective, what toxic and terrifying creatures they are! They carry infectious germs; they are nothing less than assassins of humanity!

In this situation, we no longer have the inclination to savor Kobayashi Issa's "Don't hit the fly, it's rubbing its hands, rubbing its feet."

So we bought a lot of fly swatters and mobilized the whole family to swat and kill all flies, big and small. Strangely, it seems like the flies can't be killed completely. After swatting one group, another group flies in. Their tireless spirit of persistence sometimes really amazes us. Sometimes, looking at the corpses of flies all over the ground and the overflowing goo, we don't feel any cruelty at all, but just think that this goo contains our blood and sweat, and we can't help but feel a pang of pain and resentment.

Ah! Flies! You soulless, unambitious creatures! People hate you, and you don't care. People despise you, and you don't even know it! You are such opportunistic and shameless creatures! As soon as you see something sweet in the east, you buzz and fly to the east; as soon as you see something sweet in the west, you drill to the west! You insidious, heartless creatures! You scrape people's blood, suck people's sweat, and gorge on people's fat, and yet you still want to transmit life-destroying toxins to them!

Ah, you most opportunistic, most insidious, most soulless, heartless, shameless disgusting creatures, seeing that the weather is getting colder, let's see how long you can run rampant!

Companion 301

— Ma Ying

Shadow—a lost companion:

You said, in this chaotic world, on this long road filled with thorns, shouldn't we walk hand in hand?

I think you can't deny this, and we did accompany each other in groping in the dark for a very short period of time. I still remember clearly that we were blinded by the wind and sand, our hands and feet were stabbed by thorns, we both let out struggling roars, and both of our ears could hear this sound. Then I should ask you: since you helped me so much in the past, why did you leave me without saying goodbye now?

I think you might deny all those past things, you might say that we never walked together, and you never helped me. Yes, you will overturn those things completely, leaving only me shedding tears of despair, leaving you in the distant, distant…

However, I will never forget the influence you gave me! It was you who helped me break out of that cage, it was you who led me onto the so-called road of life. This is such a heartbreaking thing, you left me on this halfway that is as empty as the land of death, and you left alone!

It's fine if you left, but why did you pretend to comfort me with that fake face before you left? You said, "Wait, I'll be back in a while." My eyes watched you leave, and my heart hoped that you would come back immediately, but now I know that you lied to me.

"Shadow! Are you really so cruel to let me fall into the abyss of despair, and let venomous snakes and beasts devour my soul? Are you willing to erase all the help you gave me before?"

I kept roaring madly. If you can hear my voice in another darkness, please come back to me immediately!

Notice to Contributors: This publication has repeatedly stated that if manuscripts are to be returned, please attach a self-addressed envelope with sufficient postage affixed. However, this is not always followed. We have recently received many requests for manuscripts. Postage stamps were initially placed in the envelopes, but when the editors found the word "return" while reading the manuscripts, the envelopes had already been lost. We hereby reiterate that return postage should be affixed to the front page of the manuscript. It is even better to attach an envelope. Supplementary Issue Editorial Office

Amateur Mailbox

Soul Flies Out of Heaven 302

— Editor

Dear Editor:

I am a young man with a weak will. After graduating from elementary school in 1932, when I was only fifteen years old, I dropped out of school and stayed at home because of financial difficulties, so I couldn't continue my studies. Later, my uncle recommended me to work as an apprentice in the Zengyu New Cigarette Shop in Caojiadu, western Shanghai. I often suffered all kinds of verbal abuse in the shop, which was really unbearable. I wanted to quit, but I was afraid that my parents would not allow it, so I just muddled through. Time flies like an arrow, and the days pass like a shuttle. It has been more than two years since I started my apprenticeship. The manager often goes against me. A few weeks ago, when he saw the toothpaste I was using, he said that I stole money to buy it. This sentence really scared me out of my wits. He is deliberately trying to harm me, making it difficult for me to continue working or quit. I am indecisive and think that I should just commit suicide. But perhaps you, sir, have a proper solution, so please give me a practical answer.

Respectfully wishing you

Peace, Wu Dade bows

Answer: It is very common for apprentices to be bullied by the boss. To commit suicide because of this is really taking your own life too lightly.

I think the problem you are facing now is not "quitting" or "muddling through," but what kind of attitude to take in the future towards the boss's unwarranted insults and grievances. If you quit out of anger, he will not suffer any loss and may even say that you are guilty of theft and have no face to stay. But you yourself will suffer the pain of unemployment and your parents' disapproving looks. What is the point of that? If, at the time, he said that the toothpaste you were using was "bought with stolen money," you should have questioned him with a spirit of sacrifice, without being vague. You should ask him: "How do you know that I bought toothpaste with your stolen money? Can't I buy it myself without stealing money? What evidence do you have to say that I stole money?" These questions should be answered by him thoroughly and concretely. In this way, even if he becomes angry and dismisses you, it is still worthwhile. This kind of "quitting" is upright and aboveboard. On the contrary, if you glossed over it at the time, then he may really think that you stole money, and soon he may dismiss you. Even if he doesn't dismiss you, the charge of being a thief is confirmed. For the former reason, your parents and friends will at most criticize you for being bad-tempered. But if you are dismissed for the latter reason, your reputation will not be good, it will be difficult to convince people with explanations, and your credibility will suffer a great loss. Therefore, when the manager unreasonably oppresses you, you should immediately protest. However, in today's society, although bosses cannot overwhelm you with "reason," they can subdue you with "unemployment," so they dare to disregard reason and oppress you at will. The method I mentioned above is only aimed at maintaining personal integrity and coping with the daily environment. If we say that apprentices can truly achieve liberation from their demands, then we must throw ourselves into the broad masses to demand a comprehensive social movement. Only in this movement can your life and freedom be thoroughly rescued. Therefore, your efforts should be divided into two aspects: on the one hand, you need to defend against the boss's unreasonable oppression, and on the other hand, you need to strive for your own active liberation.

Return 303

— by Ivan Vazov of Bulgaria, translated by Yang Sen

That autumn, a strange fog descended on the city of Vetrino. The weather was humid and cold, with a continuous drizzle. It seemed that the entire sky was melting into ice water and pouring down on the low roofs of the city. In the dark, muddy streets, there was always a noisy sound. Carts pulled by thin horses, oxcarts piled with countless military supplies, farmers leading their horses and livestock, all filled the streets. Amidst this chaos, a column of new recruits advanced noisily, some wearing military uniforms, some with only sheepskin coats turned fur-side out, and most wrapped in tattered blankets, using their eyes as waterproof cloths. They wore belts around their chests, guns on their shoulders, decorated with a bunch of boxwood, and carried overloaded food bags. These kind young men were almost frozen solid. The mud soaked their knees, and the rain and snow lashed their faces, but they still sang along the way.

At the entrance of a tavern, a group of officers, travelers, and farmers stood, curiously watching these heroes in the mud.

In the town square, a group of women, daughters, and children gathered, poorly dressed and shivering. Frozen numb. They were waiting for the soldiers from Vetrino, who were advancing from Harmanli with their joint troops to Sofia, and then being transported to the front line.

"Ah, George's son is there! Bless you, Cvetko!"

"I saw him… Languel just passed by."

"That's Nedelkin! John, your mother is here!"

"Flowers were quickly passed over, tears flowed down many people's cheeks, words half swallowed in their stomachs... The military band is coming, in fact, it has already passed."

"Mommy," a red-cheeked little daughter shouted, "Big brother is here!"

"Stoyan, brother!" This time it was a seven-year-old child shouting: he was next to the daughter, and his arm pointed to the soldiers.

"My son, my son!" The mother groaned sadly.

A tall, handsome young man with dark eyes temporarily left the column, kissed his mother's hand, and kissed the foreheads of his younger sister and brother. He wore a bouquet of flowers given to him by a girl on his chest, and another bouquet of flowers was tied to his ear. Then he rejoined the ranks and marched forward together.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Some Deviations Regarding Rural Films 304

— Mai Lang

Thoughts After Watching "As the Earth Turns"

Regarding the issue of the attitudes of film writers in dealing with rural themes, I have long had some opinions that I wanted to express. After watching Alfred Green's masterpiece "As the Earth Turns," this impulse has been rekindled.

Chinese and foreign rural film writers seem to have a common, simple concept: they view the countryside as an ideal paradise that exists in contrast to the vulgar city. In the countryside they depict, there are strong rural customs, lush flowers and trees, simple villagers, and pure love. In other words, they idealize the already dilapidated countryside into a beautiful escape for people squeezed out of the city, like a utopia. The city is dirty and sinful, so we should return to the pure and tranquil countryside. This is true of "City Lights," "Modern Times," and others.

Many people have already pointed out that the present countryside is no longer a paradise. However, the illusion of viewing the countryside as pure as a heaven, in opposition to the "sinful city," still strongly remains in the minds of many playwrights and film critics. We know that modern metropolises are not products of rational and healthy societies. The current industrial and economic systems, like magnets attracting iron filings, absorb the majority of the population into deformed cities. In modern times, cities are centers of commerce and industry, and hubs of transportation and culture. In other words, cities are places where the labor of the majority is needed for the enjoyment of a few. They absorb the rural population, turning the entire social structure into a deformed image with an inflated abdomen and withered limbs. However, in this inflated city, there are no plans to improve the living conditions of each other. As a result, because the majority of people are concentrated in densely populated areas, they form a place for fierce survival competition. Unemployment, starvation, suffering, disease, difficulty in getting married, moral decay, fights, and killings... This creates a dark side of the city like a human hell. Therefore, to be clear, sin and simplicity, darkness and light, are by no means inherent characteristics of cities and the countryside, but only temporary pathological phenomena caused by a social system. The cause of sin lies not in the city itself, but in the social system that opposes the city and the countryside. Similarly, the way to eliminate all these sins and darkness is not to "return to the countryside," but to eliminate the root cause that opposes these two. The original author of "As the Earth Turns" wrote the city and the countryside as two extremes representing evil and good (writing Jen's tranquility and purity, and Doris's frivolity and licentiousness, are all representations of the author's concept of the city and the countryside), and used the idyllic brushstrokes of a pastoral painting to depict the simple people's attachment to the land. This only shows that the author cannot deeply see the root cause of the opposition between the current society and the countryside, but simply dissatisfied with the irrationality and darkness of the city, and reactively reveals the yearning for the idealized countryside. Without a clear perspective on tomorrow, poets often seek comfort from yesterday. From fantasy to science, from empty illusions to real change, this stage of understanding must be crossed when dealing with rural themes.

The change of the social system, and the dispersion of the population caused by this change, are the fundamental ways to eliminate the opposition between the countryside and the city. Focus on reality! Hasn't there already been one-sixth of the world as an example?

Film Commentary

Review of "Sacrifice for Whom" 305

— Central Film, Ling He

Although in this script, the playwright included many technical flaws and even incorrect tendencies, in the present circumstances where it is not allowed to talk about resisting Japan, and in the present circumstances where trains and mail are open, and even the so-called economic reciprocity, we can see this film that reflects the heroic battles of the volunteer army to some extent, in any case, it is worth getting excited about. Therefore, it can further prove that our national spirit has not declined. Given an opportunity, the suppressed resentment will always erupt. Who says that film practitioners are just living in a muddle-headed way and will not awaken to fight for national interests? The small company, which has never paid much attention to the content of films, is now bravely shouldering its mission, isn't it?

But the playwright did not grasp the serious theme. Although he wrote about the battles of the volunteer army at the beginning and the end, because he wanted the audience to sympathize with the female spy, and made her sacrifice for love, the atmosphere of love-supremacism was very strong, and it confused the theme of the play. This loss is not small, right?

Regarding this point, on the one hand, we understand that the playwright had to replace the weight of resisting Japan with love in an environment where anti-imperialism was not allowed. On the other hand, in terms of creative techniques, it was completely unnecessary to make the spy sympathize with the audience. If we follow the progress of the story, that's right, we admit that a woman who lacks understanding can act as a spy for the enemy under certain circumstances, and at the same time, when she realizes it, when she knows her responsibilities, she can immediately turn to the right side. But the playwright did not pay attention to this point. He wrote her as a love-supremacist. Her transformation was only for love. This unrealistic character is the playwright's vulgarity. Then, according to this, the female spy will never realize it, so why not simply write her as a completely bad woman? So the transformation later is not needed at all.

So this woman is simply an irrelevant and unrealistic character. In addition, the director's skills are not very good, and Huang Manli cannot play this type of individualistic villain, which leads to the failure of the entire play. He, on the one hand, said that the screenwriter wanted the plot to be tortuous, so that Staff Wang was suddenly released from prison, and even the female spy's confession. That method is also very bad. Because even if the plot is tortuous, it must be reasonable.

No, these are the director's greatest responsibilities. If the director can truly take on his task, then the director must be responsible to the audience for the considerably problematic script and make it 100% excellent. The director's skills are obviously not as good as the screenwriter's skills. As we see it, apart from Zhang Yi's role being relatively realistic, the rest of the people are made to be irrelevant and unrealistic. Those roles are not inherently talented in acting, but the main thing is that the director does not understand how to develop the personality of the actors. For example, Chen Yan has always played negative roles, but here she makes her laugh when she shouldn't laugh and can't cry when she wants to cry. Huang Manli has always been a timid type, which can be fully proved in "Homecoming," but here she is asked to be a seductive femme fatale, resulting in a bitter smile on a soulless character. In addition, the director does not know the tension of the plot and does not understand the importance of tone in the play. As a result, the alertness or agility that a spy should have cannot be found on Huang Manli. He, like the director's own disguise as Captain Lu, is not very good. Only Zhang Yi is slightly better. In addition, in some places, such as inserting a medium shot in the middle of a long shot, it cannot be connected well, and the climax cannot be grasped, etc. The gimmicks are also very stiff. Other things are omitted.

American Advertising Industry Selects Best Film Advertisement 306

— Chen Xiong

In my ordinary person's eyes, film advertisements are the most prone to exaggeration and therefore the most untrustworthy. Unexpectedly, this time they have gained an unexpected harvest in the American advertising industry. This can also be regarded as a ray of dawn in our dark film circle. (Or perhaps their film circle is not as dark as China's. Editor's note)

Advertising was included as one of the Literary Excellence Awards, starting with the American Spectator magazine. The magazine presents a total of six Literary Excellence Awards each year: feature writing, satire, novel, essay, drama, and advertising. The editors of the magazine are all contemporary American writers, such as American playwright O'Neill and novelist Anderson, etc.

This spring, the editors of the newspaper evaluated the merits of advertisements from the cigarette, automobile, clothing, publishing, and stage play industries across the United States over the past year. As a result, film advertisements were selected as the best, and "Palooka" (Palooka, which will be shown at the Southern Theater soon) was specifically cited as a representative work in film advertisements. The film stars Jimmy Durante, Lupe Velez, and Stuart Erwin, and is a comedy.

The "Palooka" advertisement focuses entirely on the male lead, Jimmy Durante, with terms such as "a newly discovered beauty on the screen" and "the most musically gifted piano master of modern times." In addition, the advertisement specifically hired the first-class American cartoonist Segar to satirically depict how the male lead is a "beauty" and a "piano master," etc., so that readers are interested and must see the "beauty" and "piano master," which is the effectiveness of the film's advertisement.

After the news that the film's advertisement was selected as the best was announced, five newspaper editors also admitted that they were attracted by the advertisement to see the film, and they all expressed satisfaction. When "Palooka" is released in this city, we will definitely have the opportunity to appreciate this best film advertisement.

Speaking of Mae West, who is not attracted to her? When you read the following news, you will be even more amazed at her magic!

According to a Boston dispatch from the United States, a major theater there recently caught fire while showing a film. I cannot guarantee that this news is true. But if this is true, then Mae West is truly an amazing person!

Film Novel

Twentieth Century Limited (1) 309

— By Wen Yin

Starring John Barrymore, produced by Columbia Pictures, USA

The Twentieth Century Limited is running every day... Hasty farewells... Final kisses... Sorrowful handshakes... The station is bustling with crowds... A red carpet stretches from the entrance of the station, directly to the side of a chartered carriage. It is laid for feet that do not tread ordinary earth! Human rank differs. When the illusory dream of glory elevates one out of humanity to the lofty heights, everyone reveres them as a deity and demands that they be treated with special consideration. In years past, this red carpet was often laid for Oscar Jaffe. But alas... Oscar Jaffe has had a string of five consecutive failures... And since his utter defeat, all entrances to LaSalle Street Station have been closely guarded by detectives and police, fearing he might sneak out of the country. Because an unthinkable thing has happened: America's greatest theatrical producer has declared bankruptcy and, burdened with debt, is eager to flee. Now appearing on the red carpet, stepping lightly and frequently blowing kisses and waving to the well-wishers, is a certain Lily Garland. The rise of Lily Garland and the tragic fall of Oscar Jaffe are one and the same, inseparable. Six years ago, he discovered her. He worked with her, felt discouraged and disappointed because of her, but she, under his tutelage and encouragement, eventually became a red-hot actress. It was also he who, for three years, loved her with unwavering devotion, but he also quarreled with her from time to time and, driven by unthinking jealousy, drove her to madness, ultimately leading her to break up with him resolutely.

Owen O'Malley is a well-known Broadway newsmaker. There is also Oliver Webb, Jaffe's business manager. They are also at the station. Watching Lily's smug demeanor, they both opened their mouths, speechless. They suddenly recalled that night... When Jaffe and Lily were quarreling, they both opened their mouths, speechless. It was as if he had gone mad, rushing to the street in front of the theater, shouting at the electricians who were putting up Lily's large electric sign: "Get down! Take down the sign for me too!" Gasping for breath, he snatched a brush from a painter's hand. The painter was painting Lily's large name, trying to make it eye-catching. Jaffe dipped the brush full of black paint and furiously smeared out Lily's name on the sign. He erased the names of all the stars on all the signs. He continued to shout madly, "Cancel her name completely!" He shouted and jumped, because he could not help but perform, just as he could not help but breathe. So he shouted to the workers: "Lily Garland is no more! Return to oblivion, Lily Garland! Obscurity! Obliterate her name from the earth!" How quickly the world changes, how things have changed to such a degree! Now Lily Garland walks on the red carpet and boards the train, while Oscar Jaffe? He hides aside, waiting for a chance to sneak into the station, preparing to escape to the destitute Chicago. O'Malley, watching from the side, couldn't help but mutter a curse: "Obscurity!" Only Webb said: "What great prestige! We can use her." O'Malley shook his head and sighed: "Since she left him, Jaffe has failed four times in a row!" Webb quickly corrected him: "Not just four times, five times! I can't help but attribute it to her. When she left Jaffe, she took away all of his talent!" (To be continued)
